Local News

Japanese Repeatedly Rioted Yesterday 135

Two Arson Attacks on the Sanyou Industrial Society in the Morning

A Chinese Constable of the Municipal Council Killed, Two Injured

In the Afternoon, After the Residents' Association Meeting, They Provoked Trouble Along the Way

Attacked Shops and Streetcars, Also Injured Two Western Constables

The Sanyou Industrial Society factory in Yinxiang Port in this city was suddenly attacked around 2:30 AM yesterday by forty to fifty Japanese thugs carrying firearms, bayonets, kerosene, sulfur, and other flammable materials. They set fire to the factory. The Chinese constable at the warning station at the end of Ward Road in the Public Concession heard the alarm and notified the police station by telephone, which dispatched police to provide assistance. Unexpectedly, the Japanese thugs used sharp blades to stab fiercely and opened fire. As a result, one Chinese constable was killed and two were injured. One Japanese thug also died from a gunshot wound. At Sanyou Society, a portion of the weaving department was burned, and many weaving machines were damaged. Around 1:00 PM, Japanese residents held the Shanghai Japanese Residents' General Meeting at the Japanese Club on Peng Road. The meeting resolved to request the Japanese government to send troops to Shanghai to curb the anti-Japanese movement. After the meeting, they marched in teams and rioted on North Sichuan Road, destroying shops opened by Chinese along the road and damaging streetcars and buses. Western constables were also injured. The municipal government has lodged a strong protest with the Japanese Consulate regarding the arson attack on the Sanyou factory by the Japanese thugs. The Municipal Public Security Bureau and the concession police station have also dispatched more police and constables to North Sichuan Road to strictly guard against further incidents. The details are as follows:

Japanese Attempted to Destroy the Sanyou Industrial Society 136

Factory Site Overview: The Sanyou Industrial Society factory is located in Yinxiangxiang at the end of Ward Road in the Public Concession, which belongs to the Chinese area. However, the front gate faces south and borders the concession. The arson attack by the Japanese thugs yesterday morning occurred in the weaving department in the northwest corner, also known as the small machine room. The outside is surrounded by bamboo fences. The thugs entered by making holes in the bamboo fence. The west side is connected to Huama Road, leading to the front gate of the factory. The north side is an open space, and the northeast side is where the employees live. The Japanese thugs launched two attacks yesterday morning. The first attack was around 2:30 AM, and the second attack was about half an hour later. The situation calmed down around 5:00 AM.

Two Routes of Attack: It is said the Japanese had visited the factory area a few days earlier and surveyed the terrain. The arson attack yesterday morning appears to have been carried out from two directions. One group traveled east along Ward Road, and the other group traveled along a remote path behind the Donghua Cotton Mill. The group that came from Ward Road clashed with the Chinese constables at the No. 1 police pavilion at the end of Ward Road, resulting in three Chinese constables being killed or injured. Realizing they had caused a major incident, they immediately retreated. Therefore, the front of the Sanyou factory was not damaged. The damage was caused by the group that took the remote path behind the Donghua factory. The arson was carried out at 2:50 AM. All the fuel used was highly explosive materials such as alcohol, kerosene, and gasoline, which were placed in five or six-pound Japanese-made beer bottles. Sulfur explosives were used as ignition.

ＩP> The Sanyou Society's bamboo fence which had been broken (photograph by Huishanshi)

Sudden Fire: According to an investigation by reporters after the incident, a factory employee said that around 2:40 AM, all the employees in the factory were asleep when they suddenly heard a strange noise in the northwest corner. Then they saw flames rising from the weaving department. The factory was equipped with fire extinguishers, so they rushed out to put out the fire while also notifying the Yangshupu Fire Brigade. By the time the fire trucks arrived, the fire had already spread. The people in the factory were initially unaware of the cause of the sudden fire.

The Police Killed: The Japanese retreated along the original routes. Some who came from Ward Road arrived at police station No. 1, where Chinese constables Chen Shengde, No. 3029, and Tian Runsheng, No. 765, were on guard. Suddenly, they saw a group of people turning the corner in the dark, and another fire broke out at the Sanyou factory. They were about to use the telephone to report to the Yangshupu police station when the Japanese, fearing that the news would leak out, immediately cut the telephone line. Chinese constable Chen had two fingers on his left hand cut off and fell to the ground in pain. The glass windows of the police box and the electrical communication lines were destroyed. Constable Tian rushed out, intending to escape to the police station to report, but the Japanese followed closely. Being outnumbered, he was surrounded by the Japanese at the intersection of Linqing Road and Hejian Road, west of the Linqing Bridge. Unable to escape and fearing for his life due to the Japanese carrying weapons, the constable fired into the air as a warning. However, the gunshots only made the Japanese press closer. The constable had no choice but to fire a volley at the thugs and emptied the second magazine. He tried to reload, but he was too late. He was stabbed to death by the Japanese. As for Chinese constables No. 1116 and No. 3152, they had just left the police station to go on duty and heard that a fire had broken out in Yinxiang Port. They slowly walked towards the end of Ward Road. Seeing a group of Japanese and broken glass windows at the police station, constable No. 1116 attempted to investigate but was also stabbed and fell to the side of the gate of the Samsung Cotton and Iron Manufacturing Factory. The other constable, No. 3152, realized that the situation was irreparable and could lead to a major disaster, so he retreated, with only a minor injury to his arm. He returned to bandage himself. The Japanese snatched the gun bag, belt, and hat of constable No. 3029 and threw them into a small creek on the side of the road.

The Police Reporting Station where Constable was Harmed (photograph by Huishanshi)

Throwing Fire Sources: The Japanese used oil-soaked newspapers, sulfur, and alcohol as the source of fire. These are all flammable materials. At that time, they were thrown from below, so the roof of the weaving department was burned the most severely. In addition, the walls and other places were also burned. Afterwards, employees of the factory searched inside the fence and found many discarded kerosene bottles and sulfur packages. Some of them were collected and taken away by the Public Security Bureau of the Fourth District in the Fifth Zone and the police.

Also Shot and Wounded: Because the telephone line in the police box had been cut, there was no way to immediately transmit the news. The Japanese were able to calmly carry out the arson work. Later, the police station and the Fourth Office of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau dispatched a large number of police and constables, but the thugs had already escaped into the darkness without a trace. It is said they hid in the Donghua Cotton Mill. The Chinese constable No. 765 who died from stab wounds inflicted by the Japanese thugs was named Tian Runsheng, aged two

The Destroyed Weaving Room (photograph by Huishanshi) 137

Re-attack: About an hour after the fire in the weaving department was extinguished, the thugs returned, seemingly intending to burn down the factory's boiler room. The boiler room is located in the east of the factory, halfway between the northern furnace rooms. The west side of the furnace rooms are the workers' dormitories, separated by an alley. To the west of the dormitory, across an open field several dozen steps away, is the Donghua Cotton Mill, making it easy for the Japanese to come and go. The Japanese turned into the alley during their second attack and threw sulfur packets and explosive packets, seemingly intending to burn down the furnace room. However, the southern section was all brick walls. The outer bamboo fence hid the building inside. The fence and walls were about a dozen feet apart, so the explosives thrown by the Japanese all landed inside the fence in the courtyard, making it difficult to hit the target. Moreover, the Japanese knew that the factory was prepared, so they did not dare to stay for long and retreated soon after.

Police Converge: During the struggle between the Japanese thugs and the Chinese police, one thug was shot and killed by the police. Two were ten years old and from Shandong. The injured were Chinese police Chen Shengde, No. 3029, who was seriously injured, and Zhu Wulan, No. 1116, who was lightly injured. Both are being treated at the Municipal Council Hospital. On the Japanese side, the deceased was Ryoze Matsujuro, 32 years old. The injured were Kitatsuji Takuji and Mori Masanobu.

Court Investigation: Eleven Japanese in total infiltrated the police station and used violence to monitor the actions of the police officers within. They then cut the phone lines, vandalized all the glass windows, and joined the Japanese who were standing outside of the station, before leaving. On Linqing Road, they randomly stabbed the face and back of constable 765 Tian Runsheng, who could not bear it any longer and passed away. Yesterday morning, the deceased was carried to the forensic examination room on Feilun Road. Around 9 AM, the police reported to the First Special District Court, who assigned prosecutor Guo Huai and forensic doctors to the scene. After inspecting Tian Runsheng's body, it was determined that he had been stabbed in the face and back and died. The Western police chief briefly explained the situation that caused the incident, as more detailed facts were still being investigated, he requested a week's extension to allow time to continue with the investigation, after which he would report the details. Prosecutor Guo granted the request and rescheduled the hearing to next Wednesday. As the deceased Tian Runsheng had no family in Shanghai, the Municipal Council was instructed to provide a coffin and temporarily place the body for collection.

Police Orders: Yesterday, after the incident occurred, the Chinese constables in the Concession were extremely angry. Chief of the Concession Police, Qiu Lai, issued an urgent order, which stated that it had been discovered that a group of Japanese vagrants had attacked Chinese Constable No. 3029 in the Yinxiang Port police box this morning, and had set fire to a factory. Chinese Constable No. 765, Tian Runsheng, was killed by vagrants while he was rushing to the rescue. Qiu expressed his deepest condolences and guaranteed he would spare no effort to punish the criminals, and also assured the entire staff that the police would be particularly protected if there were any acts of retaliation against the police officers. He hoped that all the officers would remain calm and continue to serve as usual, and that the staff would maintain its inherent high standards of discipline and self-respect. In order to protect the Sanyou Industrial Society, after the headquarters was repeatedly attacked and set on fire by the Japanese yesterday morning, a special envoy went to the Municipal Government to petition, requesting the City Government to inform the Municipal Public Security Bureau and send police to the factory for protection. After receiving the news, the Public Security Bureau immediately ordered a team of more than 30 police officers to go to the factory in Yinxiang Port at around 3 PM to be stationed and maintain order.

A Glimpse of the Loss: The exact amount of loss to the Sanyou Factory is still unknown, but it has been estimated by factory staff that, including the destroyed roof and walls, along with the damage to more than 20 weaving machines, the loss is worth around 4,000 to 5,000 taels of silver. A total of seven factory buildings were damaged. Because sulfur was used to start the fire, there are many large and small burned holes in the roof, making it difficult to repair.

Factory Affairs Meeting: The Sanyou Factory, after being set on fire twice by the Japanese, convened a factory affairs meeting overnight to discuss (1) the Japanese disturbance along the way, and (2) the maintenance methods for the Municipal Council's suppression of the police vehicles and Japanese Marines.

The Japanese rioting situation near the Yokohama Bridge on North Sichuan Road (photograph by Liguang)

Page 14

Shen Jiu Cheng, the general manager of the factory, also went to the factory at 8 AM to inspect the damage. Wu Yuting, the chief of the Fourth Branch of the Fifth District, sent three police officers to the scene. By then, the fire had been extinguished. Wu also personally went to the scene in the morning to investigate. The purpose of the factory meeting was to prevent future incidents. As a result, in addition to the original fire brigade, rescue, patrol, and disciplinary teams will be formed. All the team members will be workers. Because the workers are in a dangerous situation, they will also unite with the labor union, the factory, and the guild district branch to discuss the aftermath today.

Lao's Remarks: Lao Huimin, the acting factory director, told a reporter from the Guowen News Agency that the Japanese arrived outside the factory at 2:50 AM and then carried out the arson. They first poured alcohol and set fire to the weaving room. Since it was late at night, no one in the factory knew about it. Later, the person on duty in the west of the yard came to report, and the factory's own fire brigade tried their best to put out the fire, preventing a major disaster. Not only was there a loss of funds, but also the towels and fabrics that had not yet been woven on the machines were all soaked in water and difficult to sell. The evidence left by the Japanese was taken away by the police and the Public Security Bureau for filing. This person only picked up many sulfur-wrapped cloths, which were confirmed to be Japanese fabrics upon inspection. They returned at 4:00 AM for a second time. Some say there were twenty or so people, others say there were forty or fifty. Because the factory's firefighting was not timely, it was impossible to confirm. General Manager Shen Jiu Cheng had just come over and has now returned. He probably instructed the factory's legal advisor, Tan Yigong, to prepare a document to submit to the government authorities and send police to maintain order. In short, the factory's view is that we do not hope for a victory in negotiations, because if negotiations can be won, our Chinese Eastern Province would not have been humiliated to this point. This is also something that everyone knows well. However, since this unfortunate event has occurred, we only hope that everything will not escalate from small things into big things and that the same incident will not happen again. He also said that this morning (yesterday) he heard rumors that (1) the area opposite the Fifth District was originally the headquarters of the Japanese residents, and because something happened, a Japanese machine gun team conducted drills there at 6 AM, whether for training or for demonstration, it is difficult to guess, and it is hoped that the responsible authorities will take precautions.

Japanese Acts of Violence on North Sichuan Road 138

The Residents Association After the arson attack by the Japanese thugs in Yinxiang Port, more than 1,000 Japanese held the Shanghai Japanese Residents' General Meeting at 1 PM yesterday on the second floor of the Japanese Club on Peng Road in the Public Concession. Lin, the chairman of the various road joint committees, was elected as the chairman. Yasui reported and Otsuki Shigeru gave a speech. A decision was made on the spot to telegraph their government to send more land and naval forces to suppress the anti-Japanese movement.

Marching and Demonstrating: The meeting adjourned at around 3 PM. The Japanese people were divided into two groups and went to the Japanese Consulate and the headquarters of the Marines to petition, holding wooden poles and making a fierce noise. Those going north walked along Bazhi Road. All the concession police and Japanese soldiers followed to monitor. At the intersection of Bazhi Road and North Sichuan Road, they turned north, shouting slogans.

Provoking Trouble Along the Way: When the marching team arrived at Qiujiang Road, the Japanese in the rear team had already passed Qiujiang Road and were proceeding towards North Sichuan Road. Seeing anti-Japanese slogans posted in Chinese shops, thirty or forty Japanese went to the shops on the west side of the road and used their bamboo poles and wooden bars to smash the doors and windows of the shops. More than a dozen shops had their large glass windows smashed. For a time, passersby stopped to watch, and the noise was deafening. Electric car No. 125 and bus No. 15070 going from north to south also had their windows smashed by the Japanese. The driver and passengers were injured. The names of the shops whose glass and goods were damaged are as follows: No. 663, Dade Electrical Material Factory, opposite Dade Alley on North Sichuan Road; No. 657, Dekang Pawnshop; No. 625, Yichang Electrical Material Store. The above are under the jurisdiction of the First Office of the Fifth District. On the opposite side, Tongfutai Hat and Shoe Store, Mingxing Foreign Goods Store, Tang Bailin Wine Shop, Qiaoxiang Restaurant, and Tongli Foreign Wine Shop belong to the Public Security Bureau of the Second Office of the Fifth District. In addition, No. 124, Sanyou Store, and No. 868, Hengfengchang Cloth Store, are both on Yingui Road and under the jurisdiction of the Fifth District. The losses suffered by each shop range from 100 to 500 or 600 yuan.

Assaulting Western Police: When the Japanese marched around and attacked streetcars and buses, the Western police officer Xue Bei from the Hongkou police station stepped forward to stop them but was beaten on the head by the Japanese with large sticks. Also, Western police officer No. 370 from the Diswei Road police station was beaten while the Japanese were committing violence. A Chinese named Xin Xiaojing was beaten in front of the Yunfei Motor Company on Qiujiang Road, but the injuries were minor. All of the injured were taken to the hospital for treatment.

Stepped-Up Security: After the Japanese caused trouble and committed violence, they continued forward to petition at their Marine Corps headquarters. The Public Security Bureau and police station have dispatched more police and armed military police to patrol the streets and step up security. However, the shops along the area from Bazhi Road to Qiujiang Road were temporarily closed to prevent the Japanese from intruding and causing trouble.

Sun Ke, Zhang Ji, and Others Travel to Shanghai Together to Return to Beijing 139

Wang arrived in Shanghai yesterday and will enter the capital today.

Chiang is scheduled to fly from Hangzhou to Beijing this morning.

President of the Executive Yuan Sun Ke went from Beijing to Hangzhou to meet with Wang Jingwei and Chiang Kai-shek to urge them to go to Beijing. Both had agreed, and Sun was scheduled to return to Shanghai from Hangzhou at 2 PM yesterday. Wang Jingwei, He Yingqin, Zhang Ji, Zhang Jingjiang, Song Ziwen, and other important figures left Hangzhou one after another yesterday to come to Shanghai. Sun Ke and others took the night train to Beijing that evening. Wang Jingwei originally intended to travel together, but due to the fatigue of the journey and his lack of physical strength, he rested in Shanghai for one night and changed his plans to travel to Beijing by train this afternoon or tonight. Chiang Kai-shek is scheduled to fly directly to Nanjing from Hangzhou this morning at 10 AM in his private plane. The details are as follows:

Sun and Wang Arrive in Shanghai: After the Railways learned of the news that the dignitaries were going to Beijing, Zheng Baozhao, the director of the Vehicle Department, personally went to the Hangzhou station to coordinate the vehicles. President of the Executive Yuan Sun Ke left Hangzhou first at 9:55 AM yesterday, taking a special car prepared by the Railways, attached to the early express train to Shanghai, arriving at the port at 2:10 PM, and immediately returned to his residence to rest. Accompanying him were Secretary Chen Jianru and National Government Committee member Ma Fuxiang. Wang Jingwei left Hangzhou at 1:58 PM, taking a special car attached to the medium-speed train to Shanghai, accompanied by Mrs. Wang Jingwei, Chen Bijun, and Chu Minyi. Wang and his wife got off at Fanwangdu Station and went directly to their private residence to rest. As for Zhang Jingjiang, He Yingqin, Kong Xiangxi and his wife, Zhang Ji, Song Ziwen, Tang Hai'an, Zeng Zhongming, Wang Boqun, and others, they traveled together in three special cars attached to the night express train from Hangzhou to Shanghai. Song Ziwen and Tang Hai'an got off at Fanwangdu Station, while Zhang Jingjiang and Kong Xiangxi and his wife got off at the North Station and each returned to their private residence by car.

Night Train to Beijing Last Night: At 11:45 PM last night, Sun Ke, He Yingqin, Zhang Ji, Li Zongren, Zeng Zhongming, Wang Boqun, Chen Jianru, and others took the night train to Beijing. The Railways specially sent section chief Tang Huannan to take care of them on the train. Wang Jingwei was originally scheduled to travel together, but he temporarily decided to rest in Shanghai for one night due to fatigue, and he will take the 3:15 PM express train or the night express train to Beijing today.

Chiang and Wang Meet in Beijing: When Wang Jingwei left Hangzhou yesterday, Chiang Kai-shek told Wang that no matter what, the two of us will meet in Beijing on the 22nd at the latest. Chiang had originally planned to come to Shanghai with Wang yesterday, but this plan was cancelled because Mrs. Song Meiling felt slightly unwell. Instead, he is scheduled to fly directly to the capital from Hangzhou at 10 AM this morning, and is expected to arrive in Beijing around 2 PM this afternoon.

Severing Diplomatic Relations with Japan: Xinsheng News Agency reported that President Sun had a two-day meeting with Wang and Chiang in Hangzhou. In addition to financial reform and other matters, the most discussed topic was foreign affairs, and among the foreign affairs issues, the most important was Foreign Minister Chen Youren's proposal to sever diplomatic relations with Japan. According to those who came with Sun and Wang, Wang expressed his support in principle, but he argued that the method of severing diplomatic relations and the second step of the procedure should be carefully considered. Although Chiang did not express his approval or opposition, he argued that the benefits and harms that our country would gain from declaring a break in diplomatic relations must be carefully studied. Sun believed that regardless of whether the diplomatic policy towards Japan was to sever diplomatic relations or adopt other measures, the three, Wang, Chiang, and Hu, had to go to Beijing to take joint responsibility.

Sun Ke's Speech: After arriving in Shanghai at 2 PM yesterday, Sun Ke gave a speech as follows: This time, I accepted the invitation of Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang to come to Hangzhou. The result of the two-day meeting was very satisfactory. Mr. Wang had been ill in Shanghai and was unable to enter Beijing for a time. Since leaving Beijing, Mr. Chiang was also unwilling to return to Beijing before Mr. Hu arrived in Beijing due to the temporary circumstances, which caused misunderstandings. When I met with them in Hangzhou, both gentlemen said that it was not enough to complete the situation of internal unity and unity in the party without inviting Mr. Hu to come north and enter Beijing together. However, Mr. Hu replied to the telegrams of Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang, maintaining his position as an unofficial capacity to support the government so that it could realize the responsibility of the cabinet in office and not need to enter the capital together, fearing it would involve restraint of the administration. I am extremely grateful for Mr. Hu's maturity in planning for the country and his far-sighted considerations. However, today's difficult situation is indeed not something that a few authorities in Beijing can be responsible for solving. The three gentlemen must jointly shoulder the responsibility of guidance, and the comrades in the party and the entire nation must work together sincerely and wholeheartedly to achieve something. Therefore, at the meeting in Hangzhou, Mr. Zhang Jingjiang, Zhang Puquan, Ju Juesheng, and other gentlemen all shared this view and strongly urged Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang to enter Beijing first and then urge Mr. Hu to come north. At the gathering in Chenglou last night, Mr. Chiang and Mr. Wang had already agreed to my request. Mr. Wang will leave Hangzhou for Shanghai by special train this afternoon and will arrive in Beijing tomorrow morning. Mr. Chiang is also scheduled to fly to Beijing from Hangzhou tomorrow, so from now on the central government will be strengthened, and the difficult situation can be expected to improve. As for Mr. Hu's reply to Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang, there is a saying that he will support the government in an unofficial capacity and implement a responsible cabinet. I believe that, in a broad sense, the current government was produced by the Central Executive Committee and the First Plenary Session of the Kuomintang Central Committee and is not a government established by one or two people on its own. The entire Kuomintang can be said to be in power, and there is no mention of the Central Committee members being out of power. In a narrow sense, Mr. Wang, Mr. Chiang, and Mr. Hu are all members of the Central Committee, and they can participate in the central government affairs as members of the Central Committee, and there is no distinction as to who is out of power and who is in power. I firmly believe that the three gentlemen will come to Beijing and take joint responsibility, only guiding the government, deciding on major policies, and enabling the government authorities to take the lead and then be able to take responsibility for doing things. There is no restraint on the government, so that they cannot take responsibility. If the three gentlemen, as standing committee members, who bear the heavy responsibility of the party and the country, lead the way and do not move forward, resulting in the central government being empty, causing various major policies of internal affairs and foreign affairs to be delayed and unresolved, then the government colleagues, even if they want to take responsibility, will have no way to do so, which would be very harmful. I have expressed this intention to Mr. Hu in a telegram. Mr. Hu is wise and I think he would also think so.

Yesterday's General Meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 140

Resolved to Form the Shanghai Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association

Established an Executive Committee of Thirty-Five Members, Organized by Industry

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened a temporary general meeting of member representatives at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the thorough implementation of economic severance with Japan. It was resolved to form the Shanghai Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association and to approve a 35-member executive committee, organized by industry, responsible for discussing methods to clear existing inventory. The details are recorded below. Representatives attending included those from 96 trade associations representing the money exchange, silk and satin, bookstore, coal, cotton cloth, clothing, porcelain, medicinal materials, soybean and rice, sugar, wool, cigarette, egg, rice shop, tobacco, sauce garden, north-south goods exchange, southern goods, timber, copper and tin, tobacco exchange, cotton weaving, paper, iron, electrical machinery and silk factory, department store, silk factory, watch, travel, soybean and rice trade, inland river shipping, and other industries, totaling over 250 people.

The meeting officials included the presidium members Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, Xu Ji, and Ye Huijun; Secretary Yan Esheng; Director-General Zheng Chengqing; Recorders Xue Guangqian and Wu Jichun; Master of Ceremonies Hu Weijian; and Secretaries Sun Wuqi, Xu Qing, Peng Zaizhi, Zhou Xiuquan, Jin Shengbai, Zhang Yukun, and Li Ruzhang.

After the chairman's report and customary salutations, Chairman Wang Xiaolai reported, stating that the purpose of convening this temporary meeting of member representatives was to discuss the request from seventeen trade associations to reorganize the Committee for Economic Severance with Japan into the Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. Additionally, the Dongzhuang trade association requested the convening of a business and people's assembly to provide relief to the market. Because the Committee for Economic Severance with Japan was established in July of the previous year by a resolution of the temporary meeting of member representatives, the current request for reorganization from the seventeen trade associations, after 23 executive committee meetings, should still be submitted to the meeting of member representatives for discussion. Regarding how to dispose of sealed Japanese goods, how to release wrongly impounded goods, and how to actively boycott goods in the future, it is proposed to wait until after the reorganization is decided before the Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association convenes relevant industries for detailed discussion and implementation, in order to achieve both national salvation and protection of businesses. In short, all sectors of this city have a unified goal for the anti-Japanese national salvation movement. However, due to the different nature of their professions, their efforts are directed differently. The business community is skilled in distinguishing between goods and is responsible for the economic severance with Japan, which will surely be twice the result with half the effort, he concluded.

Representative's Address Next, He Yuanming, the representative from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, delivered an address, stating that he felt very honored to attend this temporary meeting of member representatives on behalf of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department. The meaning and purpose of today's meeting have been reported by the chairman, which is to discuss issues such as economic severance with Japan. He hoped that today, under the careful discussion of leaders from various industries, a satisfactory solution could be reached. Speaking of Japan's invasion of the Northeast, all nationals are indignant. However, the methods to wash away shame and save the nation vary, and there are many paths to anti-Japanese national salvation. He then briefly outlined one or two points: 1) Prepare for resistance with real strength. According to historical experience, the Americas were able to break away from Britain and achieve independent, free, and equal status, and Spain was able to resist Napoleon's army that dominated Europe, because they had the strength to resist, and only then did they achieve final victory. Today, when we talk about anti-Japanese national salvation, everyone must first have the spirit of sacrifice in order to strengthen their strength and achieve the goal of wiping out shame and saving the country. 2) Strive to increase production, and boycott activities are the only effective weapon for small and weak nations to resist powerful nations. However, our country's boycott of Japanese goods has already occurred eight times in the past, but the failure of the results is known to everyone. The reasons are varied, but the neglect of efforts to increase production outside the boycott movement is the biggest obstacle to the anti-Japanese future. Today, when we talk about anti-Japanese national salvation, we should both strictly implement the boycott of Japanese goods and strive to increase production, so that we can counter goods with goods and implement the main purpose of economic severance with Japan. The above two points are contributed to you for reference, he concluded.

The resolution was passed.

Purpose of Establishment The Shanghai Business Community Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association announced its purpose of establishment, stating that since the incident last year in which Koreans brutally killed Chinese people, various sectors of this city have had organizations for anti-Japanese assistance to Korea. Later, as the violent Japan occupied the Northeast and spread its tyranny, it was reorganized by public consensus into the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, hoping to expand the scope and strengthen the organization. Judging from the situation in the past few months, although the effect of perfection has not been achieved due to environmental constraints, the enemy has been deeply wary and regarded it as a major enemy of aggression. Their ridicule and curses are exhausting, which is enough to prove the enormity of the injuries they have suffered. At the same time, our business community, by the resolution of the temporary meeting of member representatives of the Chamber of Commerce, automatically implemented economic severance with Japan and organized the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Committee for Economic Severance with Japan, hoping to achieve the effect of cooperative action under the unified anti-Japanese steps. Judging from the past experience of the past few months, what is revealed to us is that there are two shortcomings: one is the lack of concentration of talent. The influential figures in the business community have not been fully recruited, so the work efficiency has not been fully improved. The other is the failure to determine the powers and responsibilities and the failure of the name to be inclusive. Anti-Japanese national salvation is a common responsibility of all sectors. The situation is serious and changing rapidly. Since there is an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of all sectors to take overall charge, various professional groups should also have individual organizations within the scope of their own industries to achieve the purpose of division of labor and cooperation. Taking the precedents in this city as an example, such as the Transportation Industry Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association on both roads and the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of various universities and middle schools in the academic community, it is true that anti-Japanese national salvation is a task that all citizens should fulfill, and it is valuable for everyone to do their best. Although the organization of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this city is formed by gathering all sectors, on the one hand, each has its own business, and the spirit is inevitably restrained. On the other hand, each sector has its own strengths. For example, the industrial sector uses its spirit of daring to act and make efforts to produce and plant the foundation for national salvation. The academic community uses its wisdom in planning and considering to engage in propaganda and achieve the effect of household publicity. The business community is familiar with trade conditions and commodity identification, and prevents the source of enemy goods. If each has an individual organization within the scope of its profession, then people will be spared from wasting their time with expertise, and things will be specialized and orderly. The policies and actions of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this city are still whole, and on the one hand, it can avoid the reason for separation and delay. Moreover, the enemy's slander against our country's Anti-Japanese National Salvation cause is always that its affairs come from various sectors and organizations and have a coercive nature, and it uses all means to slander it. The general will is weak, and they deeply believe it. If this kind of fallacy is allowed to spread, it will not only sow discord and create a situation of fire and water, but the great cause of anti-Japanese national salvation may be buried invisibly. To correct this fallacy, we must change the organization and transform the plan for economic severance with Japan into a public agreement of merchants and regulations of the industry, without containing any coercive nature from the outside world. The separators have nothing to do with their skills. This is especially a great key to the continued struggle for anti-Japanese national salvation. May our business community and all sectors understand this purpose. Moreover, some outsiders may have doubts about this organization, thinking that self-protection is a basic human psychology. This organization of the business community may have the opposite effect on the cause of anti-Japanese national salvation. This association dares to tell all sectors directly that since merchants automatically implemented economic severance with Japan, such as the Textile Industry Association, the Cotton Industry Association, the Color Printing Industry Association, and the recent Coal Industry Association, they have all made every effort to report Japanese goods, or the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this city has a record to check, or the details have been seen in the local newspapers. As for the matter of merchants violating public agreements, it may also be frequent, but this is the action of private individuals, not the behavior of the group, and the association has no favoritism for these actions. What is there to fear? The country cannot therefore doubt the organization of this association because of the merchants. The above-mentioned past events can be a clear proof of the time to today. It is difficult to be afraid. People's livelihood is difficult. This association can only dedicate its blood and cooperate with people from all walks of life in the progress of anti-Japanese national salvation. On the one hand, it aims to avoid unnecessary sacrifices in the business community. On the other hand, it aims to achieve permanent success in boycotting goods. At the beginning of this resolution to organize, I would like to state the purpose to inform the society.

All Sectors Strive for Sovereignty in the Case of Coal Industry Inspectors Being Arrested 141

Yan Bin Was Found Not Guilty by Court Verdict

The Coal Industry Announces Resumption of Business from Today

Over 1,800 coal businesses in this city unanimously suspended business due to the Yongchang Coal Company's destruction of the patriotic movement and the arrest of inspector Yan Bin, as resolved by the general meeting. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Taxpayer's Association, and other organizations sent letters to the Municipal Council questioning the extra-jurisdictional arrest of the inspector and issued declarations to strive for sovereignty. The court yesterday ruled Yan Bin not guilty and ordered his release on bail. The police department disagreed and planned to appeal. The Coal Industry Association issued a notice yesterday stating that all businesses would resume operation today. The various situations are recorded separately below.

Declaration of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, through a temporary meeting of representatives, issued a declaration to assist Yan Bin, the inspector of the Japanese goods inspection team of the Coal Industry Association, who was arrested for inspecting and finding Yongchang Coal Company's private entry of Japanese coal. The declaration stated that since the violent Japan occupied Shenyang on September 18 last year, its violence and conspiracies have been advancing without end. The territory of the three northeastern provinces is entirely under its control. Our merchants and people, unable to endure it any longer, established the organization of the Committee for Economic Severance with Japan. Various industries have formulated their own public agreements to prevent the industry from privately importing Japanese goods and have established their own inspection teams of Japanese goods to avoid the few bad apples from undermining the public agreement. Since the implementation of inspections by various industries, although there have been those who dared to risk impropriety, engage in private embezzlement, and bite back, they ultimately fear public opinion and their conscience has not been completely lost. Therefore, once questioned by the public, they still know to repent. There has never been anyone as extreme as Yongchang Coal Company, a member of the Coal Industry Association, who willingly colludes with foreigners to exalt itself, destroys the public agreement of the association to stop purchasing Japanese coal, and accuses the industry of enforcing the regulations of public agreement as robbery. We want to tell this company that it should know that the patriotic people in the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, which have fallen under the iron hooves of the national enemy, are still able to organize volunteer armies and make a final stand against the violent Japan, shattering their bones and disregarding everything. We are watching the fire from across the river, hoping to share the enemy's leftovers to nourish ourselves. Anyone with a human heart cannot bear to do this. We want to tell the law enforcement officials and foreign merchants residing in Shanghai that the regulations publicly determined by the group have the obligation to force the members of the group to comply. This is a common principle of the world law. Therefore, this action, even from the perspective of the law, does not violate the essence of the rule of law and cannot be considered an obstruction to commercial freedom. Moreover, economic blockade to sanction a country that uses military force has been adopted by the international covenant and is publicly recognized by countries around the world. The exercise of this kind of national self-defense right transcends ordinary legal concepts. Friendly foreigners in Shanghai should also base themselves on international justice and broad sympathy and not be fooled by the one-sided dregs of our country, so as not to damage their feelings towards China. In short, our colleagues in this association believe that implementing economic severance with Japan is the minimum limit for the people to exercise their right to self-defense. If there is anyone who undermines it, no matter where they come from, we will fight to the end and will not hesitate to make any sacrifice. This is a special declaration.

Letter to the British Chamber of Commerce The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the British Chamber of Commerce, stating that since the Shenyang Incident on September 18 last year, the Shanghai coal industry has agreed not to import Japanese coal. This coal industry inspection team was established by the industry itself to sanction its colleagues who violate the public agreement. Since Yongchang Coal Company is a colleague and has been found to have violated the public agreement, the industry has the right to give it appropriate treatment. This matter has nothing to do with British merchants. It is regrettable that there have been reports that Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. has intervened. Since the Shenyang Incident in our country, the friendly attitude of the British government and people has left a deep impression on the people of our country, and British commercial activity with China has made good progress. This is very fortunate for the future of our country. We urge your association to advise Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. not to participate in the efforts of our merchants to sanction colleagues according to public justice, so as to avoid misunderstandings. This is a matter of great concern. This is addressed to the British Chamber of Commerce.

Letter to the Special District Court The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the First Special District Court of Jiangsu Shanghai, stating that the organization of self-inspection teams of Japanese goods by various industries to cooperate with the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in this city was resolved by the temporary meeting of representatives of the Chamber of Commerce in July last year, and letters were sent to various industries limiting the time to organize, so as to supplement the deficiencies of the Anti-Japanese Association. All industries have been organized according to the case, and the exercise of inspection powers is limited to their own industries. Since Shenyang was occupied by Japan, all firms have stopped importing Japanese coal, which has long been resolved by the industry. The industry has the right to severely punish colleagues who violate the public agreement according to commercial custom. Yan Bin, the inspector of the inspection team of the industry, is performing his duties under the order of the association. The coal obtained from the inspection is still sent to the association for handling according to the regulations and is not transferred to private ownership. There is no reason to be liable for crimes. A letter is sent accordingly for investigation. This is addressed to the First Special District Court of Jiangsu Shanghai.

Dispute of the Taxpayer's Association The Taxpayer's Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement, stating that the incident occurred in the Suzhou River, which is not within the jurisdiction of your bureau's police power according to law. Even if the coal is really the property of Mackinnon, Mackinnon should sue the Coal Industry Association and the inspector in the court with jurisdiction. The detention of Japanese goods transported by Wu Jichang is a movement of our people against the violent Japan. Your bureau has repeatedly stated neutrality, but indirectly or directly promotes the violent Japan everywhere. Is it that the May 30th Massacre, which was left unfinished in 1925, is still not enough? Or are you afraid of the brutality of the violent Japan and fear that it will repeat the siege of the Hongkou Police Station? Your bureau should immediately withdraw the public prosecution in this case in order to comply with the law and strictly maintain neutrality. Please reply to the previous reason accordingly. I hope you will check it.

Content of the Contract Lease According to the attached contract lease agreement of the Coal Industry Association, Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. and Yongchang Coal Company agreed that Yongchang Coal Company will lease one side of the warehouse to Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. for the exclusive storage of British merchant Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co.'s coal. The rent is 60 yuan, and the term is six months. After the establishment of this contract, there will be no disagreement. In order to avoid verbal discrepancies, this contract is established as proof. January 5, 1932, Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. (only a rubber stamp is affixed, without the signature of the person in charge), Yongchang Coal Company (stamp affixed below), Zhou Shumao, mediator, Yu Ruiliang, scribe.

Association Notice of Resumption of Business The Coal Industry Association sent a special transportation team to notify various coal businesses by bicycle at 6:00 PM yesterday that Comrade Yan Bin had been found not guilty by the court and that all businesses would resume operation from today. As for the coal industry market on Zhijiang Road, it is scheduled to resume business from today. The cargo loading and unloading in the warehouses in Pudong will be completely as usual from today. Resumption of Business in the Charcoal Barge Industry The City's Charcoal Industry Association believes that it is connected to the coal industry and that it is in the same boat. Yan Bin Was Acquitted and Released from Prison Amidst the Applause of Coal Industry Colleagues 142

The Courtroom Was Overcrowded

Over a Hundred People Waited for News Outside the Courthouse

The Lawyer's Eloquent Defense Lasted Two Hours

Yan Bin Was Acquitted in Court

Yan Bin (also known as Yan Bing), the investigator of the investigation section of the Coal Industry Association, was ordered by the association on the 11th of this month to investigate the private transportation of Japanese coal by the unscrupulous merchant Yongchang Coal Company, which resulted in collusion with the British firm Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co.'s manager, Mr. Mackinnon, who reported it to the Xinzha Police Station. On the 17th, the Chinese and Western detectives arrested Yan. The next morning, he was sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and was temporarily detained. All this has been recorded in this newspaper. Since Yan was detained, all sectors have rallied to help because Yan was implicated in the matter due to public affairs. The charcoal industry and the barge industry also joined the suspension of business for two days to show their determination. Yesterday morning was the date for the trial of this case. Around 9:00 AM, coal industry colleagues came to the court to listen to the proceedings one after another, so that the second courtroom suddenly became overcrowded, and those who arrived later were still coming in an endless stream. The court and the police department, in order to maintain order, dispatched judicial police and Chinese and Western detectives to guard the courtroom entrance and the stairs of the third courtroom to prevent the crowds who arrived later from entering. As a result, there were about a hundred people standing in the courtyard of the court waiting for news, and the order was slightly chaotic. The case was heard by Judge Feng Shide from 10:00 AM and lasted for four hours. It was not until 2:00 PM that the debate ended and the defendant Yan Bin was acquitted in court. The trial of this case is recorded below.

Police Lawyer's Presentation of the Case At around 10:00 AM, Judge Feng ordered the defendant Yan Bin to be brought to the case. Yan still hired three lawyers, Chen Wen, Xue Jiaqi, and Wang Zuxun, to appear in court to defend him. Then, the police lawyers Bo Liang and Wang Yaotang began to say that the police department is now accusing the defendant of conspiring to rob a lighter owned by the British firm Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. on the Mackinnon Road Wharf at 2:00 PM on January 11, containing over tons of coal worth 750 yuan, and filed a public prosecution for the crime of conspiracy to rob under Article 348 of the Criminal Law. They also detailed the course of the case, saying that the British merchant Mackinnon, the owner of Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co., had ordered 50 tons of coal from the Japanese firm Mitsui & Co. in Pudong.

Five Detained People Were Ordered to Be Released It was then reported that Mackinnon reported to the police department, which sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate the Second District Fourth Branch of the Zhabei Public Security Bureau. The director of the branch tried to bring five people from the Coal Industry Association to the Public Security Bureau. The five people, named Ye Yongfu, Ye Shengchao, Xia Yisheng, Yan Bin, and one other person whose name is unknown, all admitted at the time that they had pushed the boat away. The detectives then requested permission to temporarily detain them until 8:00 PM, when a reply would be given so that they could return to the police station to discuss the solution. When the Chinese and Western detectives inquired by telephone to the Public Security Bureau at 8:00 PM, they were informed that the five people had been released by order of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The detectives had to request the court to issue an arrest warrant to detain Yan Bin and copied out a badge.

The Police Presented Four Pieces of Evidence Now the police have four pieces of evidence to present: 1) the contract between Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. and Mitsui & Co. to purchase coal; 2) the lease contract between Mackinnon and Wu Yongchang to rent a warehouse; 3) the Coal Industry Association sent a letter to the Gordon Road Police Station admitting to the transportation of coal after the incident; 4) the Shanghai Citizens' Punishment Association sent a letter to the Laofengxiang Silver Building on Xinzha Road, threatening to destroy the neighboring Wu Yongchang Coal Company. There are also the testimonies of various witnesses presented to the court for investigation.

The Englishman Mackinnon Was Investigated Separately Then the British businessman Mackinnon testified and translated that he was a coal merchant and also ran Mackinnon Mackenzie & Co. On the 10th of this month, I ordered 3,300 tons of coal from the Japanese firm Mitsui & Co. Wu Yongchang Coal Company came forward to rent a lighter from Wu Jingen to transport it. At this point, the defendant's lawyer stood up and requested that the witnesses in this case be investigated separately. The court approved it. Then, Judge Feng asked Mackinnon: Did you sign a contract with Wu Yongchang Coal Company to rent a warehouse? He answered yes, with a monthly rent of 60 yuan for a term of six months. Asked if you had an order to purchase coal from Mitsui & Co.? He answered that because there was also a Japanese named Yimale who acted as an intermediary, there was no order. Asked if the bill of lading was given to Wu Yongchang by? He answered yes. Asked how much cargo was on the bill? He answered fifty tons. Asked where your warehouse is? He answered in the alley near 700 of Carter Road, with my Mackinnon name sign at the door. Asked where the coal ship was berthed? He answered near the Chinese Commercial Bank, near the concession. Asked when you were at the pier? Answered around 1:00 PM in the afternoon. At that time, there were two Chinese and also local news on the following page.

Page 15

Local News Two 143

A person arrived, claiming to be sent by the Coal Industry Association to investigate the goods. I questioned him about his credentials, and the two people said they had none. As I was about to arrest them, the two people then said to me, "Since the coal belongs to you, we will report the situation to the association." After saying this, they left. I waited until 1:40, seeing no movement, I declared to Chinese Constable No. 1044 on duty that the coal was mine, and then went back. Around 2 o'clock, I received a report saying that the coal had been taken away by the Anti-Japanese Association, and that the constable on duty had already left his post, leading to this incident. I immediately reported it to the police station, and so on. After finishing, the defendant's lawyer cross-examined Mr. Mac.

Yan Bin confessed the whole story. Upon questioning the defendant Yan Bing, he stated that this batch of Japanese coal was first discovered by the Anti-Japanese Association. Because the Anti-Japanese Association had no storage facilities, after discussion with the Coal Industry Association, they borrowed the Yitai Xing West Warehouse, which also belonged to a member of the Coal Industry Association. The investigation section chief, Wang, sent me to the Yitai Xing West Warehouse to register the amount of coal. When I arrived, the ship had not yet arrived, so I went along the river to inspect the area near the Sampan Factory New Bridge. I did not board the ship. Later, the ship was steered by the Tang family and others from the Anti-Japanese Association to the warehouse to unload. There were a total of ten tons and one hundred catties of coal, which are now all stored in the Yitai Xing West Warehouse, and so on.

Three witnesses successively testified. According to witness Mei Zenggui, he works as a shipmate for Wu Jingen. I was responsible for transporting the coal. The ship arrived at the Sampan Factory New Bridge and docked to unload the cargo. There were a total of fifty tons of coal. At that time, thirty-six tons were unloaded, and there were still fourteen tons. Just as we were about to unload, more than ten staff members of the Anti-Japanese Association arrived and stopped the unloading, and cursed loudly, steering the ship to the north of the creek. The defendant was not on the scene at that time. Only when we reached the Yitai Xing West Warehouse did I see the defendant and seven or eight people steering the ship together, and so on. According to witness Qi Yulin, sixteen years old, an apprentice at Wu Yongchang Company, at that time, ten staff members of the Anti-Japanese Association pointed to the coal as Japanese goods, so they steered the ship to the north of the creek. However, I did not see the defendant at that time. According to witness Wu Jingen, he gave his testimony, but was not very clear about this case and had nothing to prove.

The lawyer raised the issue of jurisdiction. The defendant's lawyer, Xue Jiaqi, then raised the issue of jurisdiction, saying that according to Article 5 of the agreement, the police station can only prosecute those who commit crimes within the concession. The place where this case occurred belongs to the Chinese territory, because the ship was docked in the Suzhou River, and the Suzhou River belongs to the Chinese territory, so the police station has no right to prosecute. According to Article 318 of the Criminal Procedure Law, it should be declared inadmissible.

Both sides debated for two hours. At this point, the witness testimony was completed. Judge Feng instructed to begin the debate. The police station lawyer and the defendant's lawyer then debated for a long time. The debate over the issue of jurisdiction was quite fierce, lasting about two hours, before each finished their argument. Finally, Prosecutor Li Ying expressed his opinion. Judge Feng declared the debate concluded and announced the verdict in court: The defendant Yan Bin was innocent. He was to provide bail within the appeal period. After the pronouncement, because the defendant's side had already prepared the guarantee, as soon as they heard the order to release him on bail, the coal industry colleagues in the audience applauded and cheered. They immediately hired a car, with a piece of white cloth bearing the words "Welcome Comrade Yan Bin out of prison" as a banner hung on the front of the car. They embraced Yan, got into the car, and sped away from the court.

Record of the Inaugural Meeting of the Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association 144

Declaration and Circular Telegram Issued

Election of Directors and Secretaries

The Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association convened its inaugural meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. 136 people attended. Shen Tianxin was publicly elected as chairman, and Cao Zhigong as secretary. First, the chairman gave an opening speech, roughly stating that in the face of the current national crisis, all our citizens should automatically rise up and find ways to provide relief. Now, all provinces should have organizations of the National Crisis Relief Association. Shanghai, being in a vital location, especially needs to organize immediately. This is the important significance of the establishment of this association. Then, the chairman read out the articles of association, and the attendees signed their names one by one. Then, the discussion began. ⑴ Discussed and amended the constitution. ⑵ Resolved to issue a declaration, drafted by Tao Leqin and passed. ⑶ Resolved to issue an establishment circular telegram, passed on the spot. ⑷ First, elected 25 directors and 3 secretaries. The remaining 10 directors will be elected in the next session. ⑸ The proposal to provide financial assistance to the Northeast Volunteer Army was passed. ⑹ Requested the government to issue arrest warrants and severely punish all Northeast military personnel and officials who collude with the Japanese to betray their country. ⑺ Sent a telegram to General Ma Zhanshan, asking him to work hard to resist Japan, persevere, and not be softened by the environment. ⑻ Publicly elected Shen Tianxin, Tao Leqin, and Hu Fengxiang as conveners of the first board meeting. The meeting adjourned at about 5:00 PM.

Articles of Association The undersigned, standing on the position of citizens, with a bright and upright spirit, and with the pure and devoted purpose of public service, establish the Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association to relieve the national crisis, complete national sovereignty, and realize democratic politics. Even if the seas run dry and the rocks crumble, this determination will not change. January 20, 1932.

Constitution Passed The Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association Constitution: (Article 1) This association is named the Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association. (Article 2) The purpose of this association is to relieve the national crisis and strive for self-defense and self-government. (Article 3) All residents of this city, regardless of gender, who support the purpose of this association, may become members of this association upon introduction by two or more members and approval by the board of directors. (Article 4) The association shall publicly elect 25 to 35 directors to form a board of directors. The board of directors shall mutually elect 7 to 11 executive directors to preside over all affairs of the association. (Article 5) The association shall establish the following specialized committees for relief of the national crisis, which shall be studied and determined by members: ⑴ Foreign Affairs Committee, ⑵ Military Affairs Committee, ⑶ Economic Affairs Committee, ⑷ Finance Committee, ⑸ Self-Government Committee. The aforementioned specialized committees may be added to when necessary. (Article 6) The association shall at any time contact people from all provinces and cities who sympathize with this association to jointly promote and carry out common benefits. (Article 7) The association's general meeting is not scheduled. It shall be convened by the board of directors when deemed necessary by the board of directors or upon the proposal of one-tenth of the members. (Article 8) The board of directors shall meet twice a month. Special meetings may be held when necessary. (Article 9) The association's membership fees shall be donated by members. (Article 10) The association borrows Room 304, 4th Floor, 4 Hong Kong Road, Shanghai as its office. (Article 11) This constitution shall be implemented after being passed by the general meeting. If it is necessary to amend it, it shall be submitted to the general meeting by the board of directors for resolution.

Declaration The Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association meets with compatriots across the country. On the day of this meeting, a declaration should be made to serve as a lesson. For twenty years, warlords have been in internal strife, and bandits have ravaged the country. This is a national crisis. Floods have caused disasters, and famine victims are everywhere in seventeen provinces. This is a national crisis. Violent Japan has invaded the Northeast region, and territory has been broken. This is a national crisis. Any one of these three national crises, as long as the country still has its people, and the people still have their country, must not be allowed to happen, and even more must not be allowed to exist. But now all three are combined. Who is doing this? Who caused it? It is the citizens who are doing it, and the citizens who caused it. The country does not belong to a few people, and the people do not belong to a few people. Citizens all have sovereignty and all have responsibility. The citizens should restrain the warlords in internal strife. The citizens should prevent the floods that cause disasters. The citizens should punish the violent Japan that invades. But now the citizens blame the government, and the government shirks responsibility. Alas, what kind of talk is this? It is a mistake, a mistake. If the citizens are capable, then the government is capable. If the government is capable, then the three ministers are capable. The capability does not belong to the three ministers, and the capability of the government is not the capability of the citizens. The capability of the citizens is the true capability. The capability of the government and the capability of the three ministers is only the capability of the citizens. The national crisis is urgent. If the citizens do not each do their best, "obligation comes first, and rights come later," the destruction of the country and the extinction of the race will be imminent. Nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood are merely empty talk on paper. Therefore, this association was founded. The colleagues of the association have publicly agreed to establish the Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association, standing on the position of citizens, with a bright and upright spirit, and with the pure and devoted purpose of public service, to relieve the national crisis, complete national sovereignty, and realize democratic politics. Even if the seas run dry and the rocks crumble, this determination will not change. This is used as a declaration for your review. January 20, 1932.

Telegram to the Government To the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Nanjing National Government: Ever since violent Japan invaded the three northeastern provinces, it has been four months now. Our country has been busy with peace talks and reorganizations, which has further emboldened violent Japan to make arrangements for aggression. Relying on the League of Nations has resulted in the loss of Jinzhou and the danger of Yuguan. Recently, it is even proposed to ask the League of Nations to use Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant and ask the United States to convene the Nine-Power Treaty. As a result, the national army has stationed troops inside the pass, making noise about salaries and sitting idle, allowing the Northeast Volunteers to run out of food and ammunition, starving and thinly clad, without providing assistance. Government officials, running around on the Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Guangdong roads, only do their best to smooth out opinions, viewing the three northeastern provinces as the people of Yue view the leanness and fatness of the people of Qin. To try not to perish is like climbing a tree to catch fish. Shanghai is the economic center of the country and the hub of international trade. Since suffering from the global economic recession, the floods in various provinces, and the violent Japanese invasion of the Northeast, business has plummeted and factories have closed one after another. Financial resources have dried up. It is difficult to describe completely. If there is no definite policy internally or externally for a long time, and only endless litigation and numerous talks are held in the court, I am afraid that it will not be enough to save the country, but will only hasten its demise. Those who are in a position to be responsible should broaden their horizons, put obligations first, and put rights later. Publish government affairs to public opinion and immediately make decisions in the people's representative organs, so that we can save the country from danger by any chance. Otherwise, if we continue to be indecisive and lack the courage to act swiftly, there will be no turning point in Shanghai's situation, and the violent Japan will only have to sit and wait to reap the fruits. This is a special telegram for your consideration. The Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association bows, seal.

Establishment Circular Telegram To Newspaper Offices and Compatriots Nationwide: Our association was established today and issued a declaration, which reads (copy of the original declaration) and a telegram to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Nanjing National Government, which reads (copy of the original telegram to the government). We urge everyone to unite in organization, take active action, and jointly seek to relieve the national crisis. In closing the telegram, we cannot express our prayers enough. The Shanghai National Crisis Relief Association bows, seal.

Directors: Wu Dan, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Xu Xinliu, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Wang Yiting, Shi Liangcai, Wang Hanliang, Zhu Yinjiang, Zhang Yichen, Cheng Zhusun, Shang Mujing, Shen Tianxin, Qian Longzhang, Hu Fengxiang, Yu Zhongxian, Li Shuixiang, Chen Peide, Wang Binyan, Yu Hualong, Wang Jiying, Chen Yafoo, Song Duomin, Hu Xiongding, Xu Yunhui. Testimony of Witnesses in the Chen Xing Marriage Dispute 145

Fu Rui Proves He Did Not Marry Yan Shufen

Sheng Sangshi Narrates Funding Chen Xing's University Education

Sang Gushi Says Both Sides Were Very Harmonious at First

Judge Urges Chen Xing to Reconcile

Miss Yan Shufen, the cousin of Yan Dunyuan, the former Minister of the Interior of the Beijing Government, was engaged to Chen Xing (courtesy name Jian'an), the recently discharged Vice President of the Central Bank, in 1912 through matchmakers Chen Handi and Ye Shuheng. At that time, Chen had just graduated from middle school and planned to discontinue his studies due to poverty. Her parents-in-law intended to cultivate him and provided him with funds to continue his studies. After graduating from university in 1919, he went to study in Jiang State, and the Yue family continued to assist him. Unexpectedly, after Chen went abroad, he married a Miss Cai in the United States, disregarding the previous agreement. After returning from the United States, Miss Yan repeatedly ordered him to fulfill the agreement and hold the wedding, but Chen repeatedly shirked and procrastinated. Now the woman is forty-two years old and it is difficult to delay any longer. Therefore, she came to Shanghai last year to negotiate with him, but Chen refused to see her. The woman then sued in court, demanding compensation for the loss of breach of marriage contract of 100,000 foreign dollars, and the 25,000 dollars advanced for tuition fees. During the initial trial, Chen claimed that Yan Shufen had written to him when she was studying at Jinghai Girls' School in Suzhou, stating that she was unwilling to marry him. Later, she married Chuan Rui (courtesy name Wutui), the nephew of the former Shanghai Daoyin, in Beijing. The amount of tuition fees assisted by the Yan family was also inconsistent with what was claimed and had been repaid after returning to China. The judge recognized that the defendant's defense was well-founded and rejected the original lawsuit. However, Yan Shufen did not accept the entire judgment and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, requesting a reversal. During one hearing, Chen, who was still the Vice President, did not attend the trial. Tao Changshan, who claimed to be working in the Ministry of Finance, and Zhu Dazhai, the assistant manager of the City Bank, came to court to testify that when Miss Yan married Chuan Wutui in Beijing, they all went to congratulate her, so the marriage was indeed a fact. However, after sending the couple to the bridal chamber, the newly married couple suddenly quarreled and divorced immediately. When questioned about Yan Shufen, she categorically denied marrying Chuan Rui. Judge Shen then ordered the two parties to go out for reconciliation and continue to investigate evidence for verification. The details were reported earlier. Now that a long time has passed, and the two parties have made no progress in reconciliation, Judge Shen Hong specially opened an investigation court yesterday afternoon to summon witnesses for questioning. The witnesses summoned were Fu Rui, Sheng Sangshi, and Sang Gushi, all of whom belonged to the appellant's side. Fu Rui originally worked in a coal mine company in Liaoning. This time, because Tao Changshan and others said in court that he had married Miss Yan, he was specially notified by Ye Shuheng to come from Liaoning to prove the truth. As for the appellee Chen Xing, after being dismissed from the position of Vice President of the Central Bank, he had returned to his hometown of Shangyu and only hired lawyer Zhang Zhirang to represent him in court, stating that since he was involved in litigation, he could only wait for the legal decision. Lawyer Jiang immediately requested the court to summon witnesses. Therefore, Fu Rui was first summoned and testified that he was forty-five years old, from Hangzhou, and was an engineer. In 1921, he was engaged to Miss Yan through his uncle. Our matchmaker was Chen Handi, and the female matchmaker was Ye Shuheng. Then, the wedding date was chosen. Unexpectedly, when the auspicious day arrived and the guests all arrived, the bride firmly refused to board the sedan chair until late at night, so the wedding could not be held. The next day, I asked the matchmaker to negotiate, but only learned that Miss Yan was unwilling to marry. I did not know why she was unwilling. At that time, relatives and friends repeatedly persuaded her, and I also believed that marriage should not be forced, so I unconditionally terminated the engagement. Recently, I learned about this case from the newspaper and learned that Miss Yan refused to marry at the beginning. Ye Shuheng also wrote to me, urging me to testify, saying that he treated Chen exceptionally well in the past and assisted him in everything. Even Chen's examination papers in his early years were prepared for him. Now that he has become rich, he has forgotten the past, stopped his wife and remarried. Please take the time to go to Shanghai to prove the truth. Therefore, I specially came to court. Miss Yan is the first time I have met her in Shanghai. I am not familiar with Tao Changshan, Zhu Dazhai, and others who came to court last time. Their statement that I married Miss Yan is truly incomprehensible. The current society is dirty. There is no shortage of people who curry favor with the powerful. Please make a clear judgment. Next, Sheng Sangshi testified that Shufen's mother was my cousin. After Chen Xing graduated from middle school, his aunt already regarded Shufen as his beloved son-in-law because his family was poor and unable to make progress, so she ordered him to continue his studies and helped him with funds. In 1916, his aunt was critically ill and left a will that Chen Xing must be harmonious with Shufen in the future and treat his grandchildren well. His aunt once said that she provided Chen Xing with no less than 20,000 yuan. Next, Sang Gushi testified that Shufen was my niece and I am her mother's sister-in-law. At first, Shufen's letter to Chen Xing stating that she was unwilling to marry was actually intended to encourage Chen to concentrate on his studies and achieve fame early. I also repeatedly witnessed the assistance funds. After Chen returned from studying abroad, his relationship with Shufen was very harmonious at first. When Shufen lived in Tianji Lane, Baoshan Road, she once hosted a banquet for him and discussed the marriage with each other. After Judge Shen questioned this point, he was very clear about the facts. He then instructed Chen's lawyer to tell Chen Xing not to be stubborn and to reconcile with the appellant. The case was allowed to be extended again for review.
